<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Reduced_petroleum_imports_and_costs">Reduced petroleum imports and costs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ethanol_fuel&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Reduced petroleum imports and costs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>One rationale given for extensive ethanol production in the U.S. is its benefit to <a href="/wiki/Energy_security" title="Energy security">energy security</a>, by shifting the need for some foreign-produced oil to domestically produced energy sources.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Turon1998_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Turon1998-89">[89]</a></sup> Production of ethanol requires significant energy, but current U.S. production derives most of that energy from coal, natural gas and other sources, rather than oil.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> Because 66% of oil consumed in the U.S. is imported, compared to a net surplus of coal and just 16% of natural gas (figures from 2006),<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> the displacement of oil-based fuels to ethanol produces a net shift from foreign to domestic U.S. energy sources.</p>
<p>According to a 2008 analysis by Iowa State University, the growth in US ethanol production has caused retail gasoline prices to be US $0.29 to US $0.40 per gallon lower than would otherwise have been the case.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Motorsport">Motorsport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ethanol_fuel&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Motorsport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><a href="/wiki/Leon_Duray" title="Leon Duray">Leon Duray</a> qualified third for the <a href="/wiki/1927_Indianapolis_500" title="1927 Indianapolis 500">1927 Indianapolis 500</a> auto race with an ethanol-fueled car.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/IndyCar_Series" title="IndyCar Series">IndyCar Series</a> adopted a 10% ethanol blend for the 2006 season, and a 98% blend in 2007.</p>
<p>In drag racing, there are <a href="/wiki/Top_Alcohol" title="Top Alcohol">Top Alcohol</a> classes for <a href="/w/index.php?title=Dragster_(car)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Dragster (car) (page does not exist)">dragsters</a> and <a href="/wiki/Funny_car" class="mw-redirect" title="Funny car">funny cars</a> since the 1970s.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/American_Le_Mans_Series" title="American Le Mans Series">American Le Mans Series</a> sports car championship introduced E10 in the 2007 season to replace pure gasoline. In the 2008 season, E85 was allowed in the GT class and teams began switching to it.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2011, the three national <a href="/wiki/NASCAR" title="NASCAR">NASCAR</a> stock car series mandated a switch from gasoline to E15, a blend of Sunoco GTX unleaded racing fuel and 15% ethanol.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup></p>
<p>Australia's <a href="/wiki/V8_Supercar" class="mw-redirect" title="V8 Supercar">V8 Supercar</a> championship uses United E85 for its racing fuel.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Stock_Car_Brasil" title="Stock Car Brasil">Stock Car Brasil</a> Championship runs on neat ethanol, E100.</p>
<p>Ethanol fuel may also be utilized as a <a href="/wiki/Rocket_fuel" class="mw-redirect" title="Rocket fuel">rocket fuel</a>. As of 2010<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Ethanol_fuel&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, small quantities of ethanol are used in <a href="/wiki/Light_aircraft" title="Light aircraft">lightweight</a> <a href="/wiki/Mark-III_X-racer" class="mw-redirect" title="Mark-III X-racer">rocket-racing aircraft</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-sdc20100426_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sdc20100426-96">[96]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Replacement_cooking_fuel">Replacement cooking fuel</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ethanol_fuel&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Replacement cooking fuel">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><a href="/wiki/Project_Gaia" title="Project Gaia">Project Gaia</a> is a U.S. <a href="/wiki/Non-governmental" class="mw-redirect" title="Non-governmental">non-governmental</a>, <a href="/wiki/Non-profit" class="mw-redirect" title="Non-profit">non-profit</a> organization involved in the creation of a commercially viable household market for alcohol-based fuels in Ethiopia and other countries in the <a href="/wiki/Developing_world" class="mw-redirect" title="Developing world">developing world</a>. The project considers alcohol fuels to be a solution to fuel shortages, environmental damage, and public health issues caused by traditional cooking in the developing world. Targeting poor and marginalized communities that face health issues from cooking over polluting fires, Gaia currently works in <a href="/wiki/Ethiopia" title="Ethiopia">Ethiopia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nigeria" title="Nigeria">Nigeria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a>, <a href="/wiki/Haiti" title="Haiti">Haiti</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Madagascar" title="Madagascar">Madagascar</a>, and is in the planning stage of projects in several other countries.<sup id="cite_ref-ceihd_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ceihd-97">[97]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Research">Research</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ethanol_fuel&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Research">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:SDethnl1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/SDethnl1.jpg/220px-SDethnl1.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/SDethnl1.jpg/330px-SDethnl1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/SDethnl1.jpg/440px-SDethnl1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:SDethnl1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Ethanol plant in <a href="/wiki/Turner_County,_South_Dakota" title="Turner County, South Dakota">Turner County</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Dakota" title="South Dakota">South Dakota</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Ethanol research focuses on alternative sources, novel catalysts and production processes.</p>
<p>In 2013, <a href="/wiki/INEOS" class="mw-redirect" title="INEOS">INEOS</a> began initial operation of a bio-ethanol plant from vegetative material and wood waste.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Bacterium" class="mw-redirect" title="Bacterium">bacterium</a> <a href="/wiki/E.coli" class="mw-redirect" title="E.coli">E.coli</a> when <a href="/wiki/Genetic_engineering" title="Genetic engineering">genetically engineered</a> with cow <a href="/wiki/Rumen" title="Rumen">rumen</a> genes and <a href="/wiki/Enzyme" title="Enzyme">enzymes</a> can produce ethanol from <a href="/wiki/Corn_stover" title="Corn stover">corn stover</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup></p>
<p>An alternative technology allows for the production of <a href="/wiki/Biodiesel" title="Biodiesel">biodiesel</a> from grain that has already been used to produce ethanol.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup></p>
<p>Another approach uses feed stocks such as municipal waste, recycled products, <a href="/wiki/Rice_hull" class="mw-redirect" title="Rice hull">rice hulls</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sugarcane" title="Sugarcane">sugarcane</a> <a href="/wiki/Bagasse" title="Bagasse">bagasse</a>, wood chips or <a href="/wiki/Switchgrass" class="mw-redirect" title="Switchgrass">switchgrass</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2016, researchers from the Oak Ridge National Laboratory used a nanotechnology-based catalyst to convert a solution of carbon dioxide dissolved in water into ethanol.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-102">[102]</a></sup></p>
